Ning-Shao Emergency Relief Association Held a Standing Committee Meeting Yesterday 100

The Ningbo and Shaoxing Associations and the Shanghai Siming Public Association, three groups that formed the Ning-Shao Emergency Relief Association for the Wuhan Disaster, convened a standing committee meeting yesterday at the Ningbo Shanghai Association on Xizang Road. Zhang Shenzhi, Shou Xiaotian, Sun Jitang, Wang Xiaolai, Hu Xisheng, Yu Qiaqing, Ge Yuchen, Shen Xiangfu, Wu Yaqin, Xu Xiajun, and others were present. Wang Xiaolai was publicly elected as chairman. A. Reporting Matters: (1) Dong Xinqin, who was sent to Hankou to escort the Ningbo fellow villagers affected by the disaster back to Shanghai on the Xinningxing ship, reported on the disaster situation in Hankou and the relief efforts for the Ningbo fellow villagers, as well as the journey of escorting the fellow villagers back to Yong and then to Shanghai, and the number of people. (2) Standing Committee Member Zhang Shenzhi reported on the reception and transfer of the disaster-stricken fellow villagers from Hankou to Shanghai by the association at the wharf when each ship arrived, and the subsequent sending of them back to their hometowns. B. Matters for Discussion: (1) Whether to send another ship to Hankou for relief. It was decided that since the water in Hankou was gradually receding and people were regaining stability, and according to the letter from the representative stationed in Hankou, it seemed unnecessary to send another ship. If there were any poor fellow villagers who could not afford to return to their hometowns, they could entrust Yin Huichang, the representative stationed in Hankou, to assist them, and the expenses would be reimbursed by the association. (2) Whether to continue renting the Xinningxing ship. It was decided to terminate the rental immediately and inform the Sanbei Company by letter. (3) The rent for the Huawu ship and the water bill. It was decided to ask Mr. Yu Qiaqing to contact the company. (4) How the expenses for the emergency relief in Wuhan should be borne. It was decided that Ningbo would bear 70% and Shaoxing 30%. It was also heard that the Yongxing ship, which was sent by the association to Hankou to rescue fellow villagers, set sail from Hankou on the morning of the 29th. Because Jiujiang and Anqing were also heavily affected by the disaster, it was feared that some fellow villagers were stranded there, so it was diverted to assist them. It is expected to arrive directly in Ningbo on the 31st. The association has telegraphed the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce for coordination.

Jianguo Ship Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday with Refugees 101

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jianguo ship arrived safely in Shanghai yesterday. According to Mr. Zhang, an employee of the ship, the details of the voyage between Shanghai and Hankou were as follows: Mr. Zhang said that the Jianguo ship was ordered by telegram to sail to Hankou to transport refugees affected by the disaster. When it arrived in Jiujiang, it encountered a hurricane and took shelter there for a day. It arrived in Hankou on Tuesday and immediately transported over 100 passengers and over 400 refugees from Jiang, Zhejiang, and Anhui. The ship carried about 700 people in total. When it sailed to Jiujiang, over 200 more people boarded the ship. Of the original refugees, over 300 intended to disembark in Anqing. However, because the city of Anqing already had 70,000 to 80,000 disaster victims, it refused to allow refugees from outside to disembark, and the entire route was guarded by soldiers and police, making it impossible for the refugees to disembark. The ship then sailed to Datong, where over 400 people disembarked. 200 people disembarked in Nanjing. Therefore, when the ship arrived safely in Shanghai yesterday morning, there were only over 150 refugees from Ningbo, Shaoxing, and Suzhou. After being taken care of by the Social Bureau, the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association, and the Siming Public Association, they were sent back to their hometowns.

Shelters in Zhabei Begin Construction 102

The municipal government believes that the number of refugees from the water disasters in various provinces coming to Shanghai will inevitably be large, and fears that there will be no place to accommodate them in time. Therefore, it has ordered the Public Works Bureau to build a large number of sheds at the foot of the Beiliuying Bridge on Gonghe New Road in Zhabei (formerly the base of the Second Regiment of the Army), commonly known as Xinyingpan, to accommodate the disaster victims arriving in Shanghai. Construction began yesterday. It is understood that there were dozens of barracks in the area, surrounded by short walls. Due to the lack of supervision, all the walls and houses were dismantled and stolen, leaving very few. Currently, in addition to slightly repairing the few remaining broken tile houses, the surrounding area is enclosed with bamboo fences. The area is very large, about 40 to 50 mu, and has become barren land. Therefore, the Public Works Bureau has ordered dozens of workers to remove the weeds. The ground is very damp, and coal cinder will need to be laid after the sheds are built. Therefore, a large number of bamboo and coal cinder have already been delivered for construction. One supervisor and two police officers have been assigned to oversee the work. The sheds are constructed with double-layered reed mats with oil paper in between to prevent leaks when it rains. The sheds are equipped with running water, and there are hospitals, fire brigades, tiger stoves, and men's and women's bathing areas at the entrance, providing everything needed. The refugees' living quarters are divided into left and right sides, and families can live together. It is said that the construction will be completed within a week, and the Public Security Bureau plans to send 50 police officers to maintain order after the refugees arrive in Shanghai.

Executive Committee Meeting of the Anhui Water Disaster Relief Association 103

The Shanghai Anhui Water Disaster Relief Association held a plenary meeting of the executive committee at Yipinxian yesterday, attended by over 200 people, including Xu Jiyu, Xu Jingren, and Lü Gaoyu. Xu Jingren presided over the meeting. The discussions included: (1) Wang Dizhai proposed that during his previous tenure in the Anhui Civil Affairs Department, the China Foreign Relief Association had a surplus of over 150,000 yuan in Anhui relief funds. Whenever Anhui encountered a disaster, a request had to be made, but the association always made excuses about guiding the Huai River and refused to release the funds. Now that the guiding of the Huai River is under the government's management, this surplus should be requested and allocated to Anhui for relief efforts. The resolution was passed and Li Cishan, Wang Dizhai, and Wang Yucheng were appointed as representatives to negotiate seriously. (2) The funds raised by the association were entrusted to Liu Zhensheng, Zhai Zhancheng, and Xu Pingxuan, who were sent by the government to Anhui as special commissioners for relief distribution. The funds were remitted to the Anqing, Wuhu, and Bengbu Chambers of Commerce for collection and distribution by various counties, selecting those in urgent need. The resolution was passed. (3) The Anhui Provincial Government was requested to issue 5 million yuan in disaster relief bonds, which would be used exclusively for emergency relief and not diverted to other charities or other purposes. The resolution was passed. (4) Disaster victims in various counties were in urgent need of food, and the government was unable to provide for them daily. The provincial government was requested to strictly order various counties to properly appease and assist them. The resolution was passed. (5) The Beijing Fellow Villagers Association sent a letter stating that Fang Yushan was privately profiting from over 300,000 yuan in Tianjin-Pukou Railway stocks and interest, which were earmarked for Anhui public welfare, and was refusing to hand them over. It was resolved to pursue and release them for emergency relief. (6) Xu Jingren, Kai Yunnong, Li Cishan, Xu Jiyu, Hong Zhenjiu, Li Zhenya, and Cao Zhigong were elected as representatives to liaise with relief organizations and charities. The resolution was passed. (7) The chairman reported that the Shanghai Bank had donated 6,000 yuan, which had been allocated to the association. Fundraising was still ongoing, and the committee members present made pledges and volunteered to solicit donations. Song Bangding, a weaving worker, donated 50 yuan, which he had saved from years of hard work, moving the audience and prompting even more enthusiastic donations.

He Xing Office Donates Wages to Relief: The He Xing Office of the Shipbuilding Industry Union in the First District, initiated by Mr. Long Peiyun, convened a meeting of all team leaders to discuss water disaster relief and resolved that all factory workers would donate half a day's wages to relief efforts.

Prostitute Xiao Lin Daiyu Donates 100 Yuan: Xiao Lin Daiyu, a prostitute from Qunyu Fang on Shantou Road, personally delivered a donation of 100 yuan to the Renji Hall Urgent Relief Association yesterday, requesting that it be distributed.

Proper Method Needed for Distributing Relief Cakes: A letter from the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association to the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Water Disasters in Various Provinces states: "We are writing to inform you that our members have reported seeing many charitable people purchasing large quantities of cakes to send to the disaster area for relief. However, due to the thickness of the cakes and the bakeries' rush to deliver, they are often raw inside. These charitable people, not having time to wait for them to cool, pack and transport them immediately. By the time they arrive in the disaster area, they are already moldy. Disaster victims, with long-empty stomachs, do not consider hygiene and often become ill and die after eating them. Thus, these charitable individuals inadvertently cause harm while intending to do good. Our association, upon receiving this report and confirming its accuracy, is writing to request that your association promptly devise a proper method to guide charitable people who go alone to distribute relief, which is our sincere hope."

Lawyer Yao Jian's Suggestion: Lawyer Yao Jian, a member of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, recently submitted a letter to the Shanghai Lawyers Association, requesting that it be proposed and resolved. He wrote that this year's water disaster in China has affected 80 million people. Although the government has issued 80 million yuan in public bonds, this averages only one yuan per person. While the people are happy to donate, it is difficult to reach 80 million yuan. The government should accept any policy that does not harm the country's vitality. He observed that the recent increase in crime has filled prisons in various provinces, wasting national funds. To rescue disaster victims, prison food should be used. All those sentenced to less than five years, regardless of gender, whether their cases have been decided or not, should be allowed to commute their sentences to cash, with a temporary commutation regulation set at one or three yuan per day, effective from this month. This would average 1,000 yuan per person, and 10,000 people would yield 10 million yuan. (The number of criminals in the Shanghai Chinese Concession and Settlement exceeds 10,000.) The whole country could generate over 80 million yuan. Those sentenced to more than five years, except for those guilty of capital crimes and banditry, should be sent to the disaster areas to perform river-management labor, with one day of labor offsetting two days of imprisonment. This would empty the prisons, bringing harmony to the world, and prison food could be used for relief. Those who commute their sentences can work in society and contribute to production. The country establishing a commutation regulation for disaster victims is more honorable than previous national day amnesties. Redemption is permitted by ancient laws and should leave no regrets for future generations. It would also gain the respect of other countries, who would recognize the government's emphasis on the people's lives. 60% of the funds should be used for relief, 10% to purchase river-dredging machinery, starting dredging from the outlet, 10% to purchase drainage machinery, 10% to purchase new-style agricultural tools for mechanized planting and harvesting, and 10% to purchase seeds and scientific instruments for chemical farming to increase yields. What do you think of this opinion? Please propose a resolution and forward it to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for approval and implementation.

Amidst the Water Disaster

Stagnation of Shanghai's Industries 107

Merchants Inevitably Show Worry

Greatest Impact on Woolen and Foreign Goods

Since the beginning of autumn, continuous heavy rains have caused floods in various regions, with breaches in river channels frequently reported. The most severe are in Wuhan and Shaobo in northern Jiangsu, where hundreds of thousands of people have drowned, an unprecedented event in recent centuries. People across the country have risen to provide disaster relief. Shanghai, as a commercial port with thriving businesses, leads the country. August and September are usually the time when autumn goods are launched, and merchants from various regions come to Shanghai to purchase goods. Due to the floods, merchants have stopped coming to Shanghai, and those with branch offices in Shanghai have also received telegrams to stop purchasing goods. Freight transport has completely stopped in Gaoyou, Shaobo, Xinghua, Yancheng, Dongtai, Bao Ying, Tai County, Funing, and along the Yangtze River in Wuhu, Anqing, and Jiujiang. The volume of goods purchased by merchants from Wanxian, Yichang, Tianjin, and Niuzhuang has also been greatly reduced due to the floods. As a result, all industries in Shanghai inevitably show worry, anticipating that there will be no recovery in business this autumn. The greatest impact is on the woolen and foreign goods industries, followed by general merchandise, and then silk and dyes.

Difficulty Reorganizing Shanghai's Grain Storage Funds 108

The Jiangsu Department of Civil Affairs previously sent personnel to Shanghai to investigate grain storage matters. It is now reported that the department has instructed the county to thoroughly reorganize. The department has stipulated measures that require counties where grain storage funds have been misappropriated to investigate and identify those who misappropriated the funds, issue warnings in the newspaper, and set a deadline for repayment. However, the situation regarding the misappropriation of grain funds in Shanghai County is unique and different from other counties. During the Qi-Lu War, over 100,000 yuan from the grain storage fund was misappropriated for military use. At that time, Shen Zhou, the deputy director of the former fund property office, insisted on protecting the funds for famine relief and argued strongly with the military headquarters, even leading to his detention. He was eventually released through the efforts of various gentry, but the funds were still taken away. Later, there was talk of repayment from the proceeds of the sale of the arsenal, but the sale has been cancelled and is no longer an option. Those concerned about famine relief should consider how to recover these funds.

Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds

Collection Begins Today 109

Custody Committee Entrusts National Products Bank to Distribute

Collection Requires Certification from Executive Committee

The four million yuan for the Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds for symptom relief has been issued by the Ministries of Finance and Industry. The Shanghai and Wuxi Silk Merchants Association of Zhejiang Province convened a representatives' meeting to report on the process of applying for the public bonds. The bonds have been received by the fund custody committee and will be issued by the trust department of the National Products Bank starting today. Details are as follows:

Issuance Notice: The Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds Fund Custody Committee issued a notice to manufacturers yesterday, stating: "The four million yuan in bonds for symptom relief under the Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds has been issued by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry to this committee. One copy each of the Shanghai, Wuxi, and Zhejiang investigation summary tables has been issued, instructing immediate distribution according to the amounts listed in the roster. The trust department of the National Products Bank at 3 Hankou Road is entrusted to handle the distribution from 9:00 a.m. to 12:00 noon and from 2:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. daily, starting from August 31st. Silk merchants eligible to receive bonds must first present a certificate from the executive committee, then verify that the seal matches, and fill out a declaration before collecting. To ensure full awareness, this notice is hereby issued."

Collection Procedures: Silk manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces who are eligible to receive bonds must first fill out a collection letter with the industry association, which is then reviewed by the chairman of the industry association (Shen Huachen in Shanghai, Chu Huiseng in Zhejiang, and Qian Fenghao in Wuxi), who is also a member of the Silk Industry Public Bonds Executive Committee, to verify eligibility and that the information is correct. A certificate is then issued, which the manufacturer takes to the trust department of the National Products Bank, entrusted by the fund custody committee, to collect according to the allocation standard for each spinning wheel. After verification, a collection slip is filled out, stamped, and exchanged for a copper token from the trust department. The manufacturer uses this copper token to claim the bonds.

Shipping News Amidst the Boycott 110

Stopping the Sale of Rapeseed: Wuhu rapeseed is mainly exported to Japan. Since the boycott, Japanese merchants have been rushing to ship their purchased goods to Japan. In recent days, Nisshin Yangtze River ships arriving in Shanghai have been carrying a large amount of rapeseed, which is being transshipped to Japan through the Japanese postal service. Currently, there are still 38,000 packages of rapeseed in Wuhu that have not been loaded for export. Upon receiving this information, the Anti-Japanese Association has telegraphed Wuhu to stop selling the goods to Japanese merchants and to stop loading them.

British Merchants Add Ships: Since the boycott of Japanese ships and the lack of Chinese ships sailing on the South China route, Jardine Matheson has achieved a dominant position in import and export trade in Shantou and Guangdong. Following the recent loss of the Guang Sheng and the grounding of the Wei Sheng, the company telegraphed its Hong Kong headquarters to send the 3,000-ton ocean liners Daweigen and Sandagen to Shanghai to operate exclusively on the Shanghai-Shantou-Guangdong route, with the first voyages scheduled to begin on September 2nd.

No Cargo on the Yangtze River: Chinese merchants have effectively stopped loading Japanese ships on the Yangtze River route. The Nisshin Company's Xiangyang Maru ship has no cargo loaded from Shanghai, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Wuhu, and Jiujiang. It has only twelve pieces of general merchandise in Hankou, making it virtually empty. The shipping industry has been the most affected by this boycott.

Request to Transfer Crew Members: The Zhengji Company's merchant ships total more than twenty. Because the head office is located in Dalian, the captains, first officers, and second officers on each ship have historically been Japanese. After the rise in the value of gold last year, the salaries of the captains, first officers, and second officers, which are calculated in Japanese yen, have greatly increased the expenditure in national currency, totaling more than 300,000 yuan in losses. During the current nationwide boycott, the company has decided to replace the Japanese crew members on each ship with Chinese nationals, both to save on salaries and to express patriotism. The company has telegraphed the Shanghai Shipping Association, requesting assistance in finding shipping professionals with coastal experience to serve as captains and replace the Japanese. The Shipping Association believes that this matter concerns sovereignty and requires a large number of qualified personnel, so it has telegraphed the Ministry of Communications for instructions and requested recommendations.

Hydrographic Office

Receives Customs-Operated Surveying 111

Since the Navy Hydrographic Office took charge of national waterway surveying, it has been systematically surveying the country's rivers and coasts. However, the waterway from Toutou Chun at the mouth of the Yangtze River to Liancheng Zhou in Jiangyin, specifically from 122 degrees 9 minutes 30 seconds east longitude and 31 degrees 0 minutes 36 seconds north latitude to 122 degrees 0 minutes 12 seconds east longitude and 31 degrees 59 minutes 24 seconds north latitude, has been surveyed by special teams from the Customs using the Liujin ships to manage taxation. This arrangement is unprecedented in the world. Recently, the matter was approved by the National Government after being submitted by the Navy, and the Ministries of Finance and Navy were instructed to order the Customs to transfer this survey work to the Hydrographic Office. All Customs funds, equipment, files, charts, and related items for surveying the area should be transferred to the Hydrographic Office for continued operation. Transfer procedures are currently underway to facilitate active operations. The area is the gateway to the Yangtze River, with very frequent ship traffic and rapid changes in water flow and sandbars. To ensure navigational safety, the Hydrographic Office has dispatched the Jiao Ri and Jing Xing ships to conduct surveys and has published revised charts for various sections, including Baoshan to Baimao Sha, Tongzhou Waterway, Langshan to Longtan Port, and Longtan Port to Liancheng Zhou. The survey of the Yangtze River mouth to Wusong Waterway has also been completed and will be published soon. The accuracy and detail of these charts have been praised by shipowners. Further surveys will be conducted and charts published to benefit safe navigation.

Social Bureau's Notice Yesterday

Labor-Management Dispute Both Parties Comply 113

Those Who Disobey Summons

Should Be Subject to Appropriate Fines

The Municipal Social Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that those who intentionally disobey summonses in labor-management disputes should be subject to appropriate fines. The notice states that labor-management disputes are already a social malady. If one party petitions for mediation and the other intentionally refuses to attend, causing prolonged disputes that harm both sides, it is especially inappropriate. The bureau, recognizing the worsening habit of parties in labor-management disputes intentionally disobeying summonses, has drafted measures for punishment and submitted them to the Municipal Government's Instruction No. 11643, which states: "The implementation of assessing appropriate fines for parties in labor-management disputes who intentionally disobey summonses should be handled by the relevant administrative office. Please comply accordingly." In addition to complying with this from today onward, this notice is issued to both labor and management in the city for full awareness.

Following the Western Restaurant Strike

Social Bureau to Mediate Tomorrow 114

Has Asked the Court to Compel the Employer to Attend

Union Executive Arrested and Sentenced to Four Months

Following the Western restaurant workers' strike on the 12th over treatment and conditions, Western chefs joined the strike in solidarity. The employer reportedly defied government orders and refused to resume work, causing delays until now. The Social Bureau has scheduled mediation for tomorrow. Details are as follows:

Mediation Proceeding: Because the Western Restaurant Industry Association defied government orders, refused to resume work, and intentionally failed to attend, causing prolonged disputes, the Social Bureau notified the Western Restaurant Workers Union yesterday, stating: "Regarding the labor-management dispute over treatment and conditions, this bureau has scheduled a hearing for 9 a.m. on September 1st. This notice is hereby issued to the union, instructing it to designate two responsible representatives to attend the hearing." A letter has also been sent to the Special District Court, compelling the responsible person of the Western Restaurant Association to attend the hearing.

Executive Arrested: Li Zuoheng, the executive director of the Western Chefs Union, was arrested on August 20th at the Yizhi Xiang Western Restaurant on Fourth Avenue for persuading non-union members not to disrupt the labor movement. He was detained by the Old Zhabei police station and handed over to the Special District Court for trial. He was sentenced to four months imprisonment the day before yesterday. The union claims that the executive was acting legally and has declared its dissatisfaction, retaining lawyer Xi Yuchang to file an appeal and petitioning the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Social Bureau to request the court to release him.

Labor Community Support: Over twenty unions, including the municipal water and electricity, pharmacy, hat-making, umbrella, pharmaceutical, dyeing, sauce, and cigarette industries, have declared that the Western restaurant employer defied government orders, refused to resume work, and disregarded the livelihood of the workers. They have issued declarations and petitioned the responsible authorities to punish the employer and promptly convene mediation to save over five hundred workers from their plight.

Nisshin Textile Mill

Obstructs Workers from Organizing a Union 115

Guomin News reported that over 3,000 workers at the Nisshin Textile Mill in Pudong established a union in May of 1925, when the May Thirtieth Massacre occurred. Later, the factory used reactionaries to control union affairs, leading to the collapse of union work and its de facto suspension. Seeing the union disintegrate, the factory increased the workers' workload to twelve hours per day, did not stop work on revolutionary memorial days, did not pay wages, and arbitrarily dismissed workers. All enthusiastic members who had previously served the union were dismissed. The workers' suffering is beyond description. Recently, workers at the mill, unable to endure the factory's oppression, petitioned the party and government authorities, requesting relief from their suffering. The Fifth District Cotton Textile Industry Union appointed Huang Linxiang and others as preparatory members for the Nisshin Textile Mill branch office and were posting notices to inform the workers to register. However, the Japanese in the factory obstructed them, tore down the notices, and forbade posting them. They ordered the foremen to identify workers and forbid them from registering. At the same time, they hired over a hundred people to monitor the workers' movements. A certain enthusiastic worker surnamed Huang from the cleaning workshop's steel wire department was seen leading workers to register, reported to the factory by those hired by the factory, and subsequently punished with a three-day suspension. Upon hearing this news, the workers in the department, angered by the factory's illegal oppression, were all stirred up and will take serious action. The union has petitioned higher authorities to send personnel to seriously negotiate with the factory and to arrest and punish those used by the factory according to the law.

Local News Two

Public Security Bureau Water Patrol Team

Seizes Large Quantity of Military Arms 126

Smugglers Dared to Open Fire and Resist Arrest

Six People Arrested and Taken to Public Security Bureau

On the morning of the 29th of this month, at approximately 2:00 AM, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team cracked down on a large quantity of firearms in the Yangshupu river area in northern Shanghai. At that time, the smugglers dared to open fire and resist arrest. Fortunately, the officers and police of the team bravely stepped forward and were able to capture the witnesses and evidence and take them to the bureau for interrogation. The details are recorded on the left:

On the evening of the 28th of this month, at approximately 9:00 PM, Water Patrol Team Captain Xu dispatched Patrol Officer Li Chenghua, along with team members Zhang Dianchen, Song Deyun, and others, to patrol the jurisdictional area. The following day (29th), at approximately 2:00 AM, Patrol Officer Li and others were patrolling the river area off Yangshupu in northern Shanghai when they saw a French merchant ship moored in the middle of the river. A barge was alongside it, and sacks were being unloaded from the ship onto the barge. However, the actions of the people on the barge were strange. Patrol Officer Li and others became suspicious. Just as they were about to patrol closer to investigate,

More than Ten Shots Fired Suddenly, they heard two gunshots from the French merchant ship. The patrol officers became even more suspicious and immediately approached the ship. However, the people on the ship fired more than ten shots at the officers, one bullet hitting a police officer's hat, while the rest hit the deck, fortunately without injuring anyone. They then threw a sack into the river. The people on the barge alongside were alarmed and immediately sailed away. The police bravely pursued and managed to intercept the barge on the spot.

Seized Military Arms Patrol Officer Li and others immediately boarded the barge and conducted an inspection. They found nine sacks in the cabin, which, when opened, revealed Browning pistols and Browning pistol bullets, bullet clips, etc., as well as one Mauser pistol and one hundred Mauser pistol bullets. As the matter involved the smuggling of a large quantity of firearms, they immediately arrested the barge crew members Mao Jinkai, Zhang Chengkui, and Xun Henian, Tang Guicai, Su Guifu, Yang Wanhe, and others, and sent the witnesses and evidence to the Water Patrol Team.

One Sack Retrieved Captain Xu then dispatched Liu Qimin, an officer from the First Squad, Lujiazui Police Station, along with Police Chief Chen Baozhen, to the scene of the incident to retrieve the sack thrown from the French merchant ship. After about four hours, the sack was retrieved. When the sack was opened, many more bullets were found and taken back to the main team.

Statements from the Crews of Both Ships During the preliminary interrogation by Captain Xu, barge crew member Mao Jinkai, 34 years old, from Yancheng, stated that on the afternoon of the 28th of this month, at approximately 6:00 PM, a Mr. Huang from Guangdong instructed him to sail the barge to Yangshupu that evening to transport goods. Due to business reasons, he complied and sailed the barge to the French merchant ship in the middle of the Yangshupu river. Before long, Mr. Huang unloaded many sacks from the ship. He caught sight of the police team arriving and quickly steered the boat away to avoid them temporarily, but was still arrested. Zhang Chengkui, 45 years old, from Yancheng, stated that his statement was similar to Mao's.

Case Sent to Public Security Bureau During the interrogation, Xun Henian, 31 years old, Tang Guicai, 32 years old, Su Guifu, 31 years old, and Yang Wanhe, 21 years old, all stated that they were from Yancheng and worked as inspectors on the Shunheng Steamboat. Recently, they had important business together and hired Mao's barge from Pudong to cross the river. Mao suddenly sailed the barge close to the French merchant ship and transported sacks. They were impatient and urged him to leave quickly. They were then apprehended by the police team. However, they all denied knowing anything about the smuggling of firearms. As the case was important, they were instructed to prepare documents and send the six arrested individuals, along with the seized military arms, to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Special Telephones Installed at Important Intersections

According to the "Continental Daily," in order to obtain timely information and facilitate arrests, the Public Concession Police Department installed police-only telephones on telephone poles at important intersections yesterday (29th). Daughter-in-Law of Salt Merchant

Accuses Husband's Brother of Seizing Property 128

Husband Suffering from Mental Illness

Inheritance Managed by Husband's Brother, Shi Ying

Monthly Household Expenses Not Provided

Zhang Yeting Forced to Sue

Woman Zhang Yexiu, from Nanjing, 39 years old, residing at No. 13 Mingwa Lane, Nanjing, is the ninth daughter-in-law of the famous salt merchant Zhang Shaotang. Zhang Yexiu is now suing her husband's brother, Shi Ying, for seizing all the inheritance. She has hired three lawyers, Xu Bingcheng, Yu Naiheng, and Xu Fuji, to file a criminal self-indictment in the First Special District Court, requesting that he be punished for breach of trust and embezzlement under Articles 366 and 356 of the Criminal Code. The lawsuit is recorded as follows: (Excerpt above) The ninth son, Shi Kun, of the late Zhang Shaotang, was married to the plaintiff. All of the late Shaotang's inheritance, in December of the eighth year of the Republic [1919], was divided among the eight branches of the family by relatives, with each branch receiving its share and managing it independently. However, the plaintiff's husband, Shi Kun, suffered from a mental illness, which would come and go, and was unable to manage affairs. His share of the inheritance was managed by his brother, Shi Ying (of the seventh branch). It was said that after managing the property of the ninth branch, he would make it a huge fortune in ten years. As Shi Kun suffered from mental illness, he had no say, and the plaintiff did not suspect any ulterior motives, so she deeply trusted him. However, after Shi Ying took over the management of the property, he first limited the plaintiff's household expenses to only 200 yuan per month. Later, as the population grew and household expenses increased, she repeatedly requested that it be gradually increased to 400 yuan. By 1928, when her eldest son, Zonggu, married into his wife's family, she asked Shi Ying for funds, but he refused, claiming he had no money, and sold the ancestral property under her husband's name to pay for Zonggu's marriage. The plaintiff, considering the relationship, tolerated it. Shi Ying, seeing that the plaintiff had given in, thought she was easy to deceive. Whenever the plaintiff had special expenses, he would blackmail her in every way, refusing to issue the funds. If she argued with him, he would become angry. Since January of 1930, he has not provided a single cent of the 400 yuan monthly household expenses. Although relatives have tried to persuade him in every way, it has been to no avail. Shi Ying clearly knows that all of the property of the ninth branch is in his hands, and he abruptly stopped the living expenses for a minor reason. Upon investigation, Shi Ying manages Shi Kun's property in two parts, public and private. Regarding the private property, just in terms of the rice fields, the amount of rice harvested and the price of rice sold differ greatly each year compared to the adjacent fields. Moreover, the items listed in his report are very vague, and there are countless contradictions. As for the public property, just in terms of the Yihexiang Salt Company, since its opening until Shi Ying took over, there was a surplus of more than 480,000 yuan. After he took over, the annual business situation, according to custom, should have been reported in a red list or listed in a report at the end of each year for verification. However, since Shi Ying took over, there has been no paper or word. The other branches receive funds from Yihexiang completely based on Shi Ying's emotions, with those he likes receiving more and those he dislikes receiving less, with the former receiving 80,000 to 90,000 yuan and the latter receiving 30,000 to 40,000 yuan, but the plaintiff's husband receives a dividend of only a few thousand yuan. As the salt company is jointly owned, all profits should be distributed equally among the branches, but now they are disproportionately light and heavy, which is clearly embezzlement. Based on the facts stated above, Zhang Shi Ying is truly deserving of punishment. She hereby submits a petition requesting a warrant to summon the defendant to court to be punished according to the law.

Li Zhaohuan and Guo Chengen Both Gave Speeches

All alumni of Jiaotong University who serve on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, in view of the fact that they are usually scattered in various places and their feelings need to be connected, elected three preparatory committee members in the first half of the year to prepare for the establishment of the alumni association of Jiaotong University on two railways. The "Yang Yongtai" Sandboat Encountered Hurricane Disaster 130

The Ship Hit the Beach and the Cargo Was Lost

People Scattered and Returned in a Wretched State

The "Yang Yongtai" sandboat of Beiyang recently loaded soybean oil and other northern goods from Dalian and set sail back to Shanghai. However, during the recent hurricane, the "Yang" ship was sailing on the Zhishan sea. The crew members saw that the situation was fierce and the waves were turbulent. They were about to look for a port to anchor and avoid the wind, but a gust of wind and waves struck, breaking the ship's rudder. Then the bow mast was blown off by the strong wind. The crew members were panic-stricken. At the same time, the three crew members working at the bow were swept into the sea by the waves. The crew members were helpless and had to retreat to the cabin. Suddenly, the ship was driven by the wind and waves to the Fushan estuary beach in Nantong, where it overturned and ran aground on the beach. The hull was smashed. The crew members called for help for a day and a night, but no ship came to the rescue. The ship was flooded. The next morning, when it dawned, the crew members used the small sampan on the ship to reach the beach. Several crew members were squeezed into the sea while rushing to get on the sampan. The shipowner and several crew members used the sampan to reach the Fushan seaside and stayed on the hillside for two days. It was not until the sea calmed down on the 27th that a fishing boat sailed past and called for help. The fishing boat rescued the crew members of the "Yang" ship, carried them to Liuhhe. The crew members had no food or drink for three or four days after the disaster. The sandboats moored in Liuhhe learned of the disaster and provided meals and clothing. The charity provided clothing. The ship had 21 crew members, and the shipowner found nine people missing. The crew members are currently staying in hotels. Yesterday, the shipowner and three crew members took a train from Wusong to Shanghai to report to the owners and cargo owners. It is reported that the ship was smashed in the middle and is useless. The water level has been rising in recent days, and although the ship is aground on the beach, it is likely to be submerged. The ship and cargo are worth 120,000 to 130,000 taels. The owners have hired a ship to go and inspect, but it is unknown whether it can be salvaged.

Fingerprints Must Be Taken of Male and Female Corpses 131

The Municipal Public Security Bureau issued an order to all district stations and teams yesterday that in the future, for any unidentified male or female corpses found in the city, in addition to notifying the local police and reporting to the local court for examination as usual, a police officer specializing in fingerprinting should be dispatched to take fingerprints of the corpse's hands for record and verification.

Robbery and Injury on Caishi Road 132

Woman Shao Yueying Not Seriously Injured

At No. 104 Renshou Lane, Caishi Road, at 12:00 last night, two robbers suddenly broke in and robbed the home of Chen Chuangming. Chen and his wife, Shao Yueying, were awakened from their sleep. The robbers robbed Chen of five or six yuan in cash. Not satisfied, they wanted to search for more. Chen's wife shouted to stop them, and the robbers fired a shot, piercing Chen's wife's right arm. The two robbers then fled. Chen's wife was taken to Baolong Hospital for treatment. Her injuries were not serious.

A Paper Package Found in an Alley 133

Seemed to Be Opium… Sent to the Police Station

Before about 8:00 AM on the 29th, a square paper package was found behind the Dehe Gongji indigo shop in Qunyi Lane, No. 450 Ningbo Road. The shop's clerk thought it was something lost by someone else and took it to the shop to wait for the owner to claim it. However, by 3:00 PM yesterday, no one had inquired about it. The clerk then reported to the shop's executives, who opened the package and found 17 small packets, which seemed to be opium. They then sent a letter to the Zhabei Police Station.

Buying Scrap Copper

Two Sacks of Cartridges Bought 134

The Yufeng Copper and Tin Shop at No. 19 Wanzhu Street in the city recently purchased several sacks of scrap copper from somewhere. However, two of the sacks contained gun cartridges and many bullets. At noon yesterday, this was discovered by the Second District, First Precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. They immediately dispatched a patrol officer and police chief to search the copper and tin shop and found many bullets and cartridges. They arrested the shop clerk and confiscated the two sacks of bullets and cartridges. The investigation into whether there are other circumstances is currently underway.

Investigation of the Huang Haitang Assassination Case Concluded 135

Sentencing Scheduled

Huang Haitang, a native of Hubei, 40 years old, residing at No. 155 Tongzhou Road, was stabbed in the abdomen with a knife at the Xiaocai Market on Pingliang Road at 11:40 PM on the 20th of this month while lying on the ground for cooling down. Huang endured the pain and reported to the police, accompanying them to No. 512 Yangshupu Road, identifying Zhu Yuting, a native of the same province, as the assailant. He was arrested and taken to the Yangshupu Police Station. Wang Haitang was sent to Tongren Hospital, where he died due to his injuries. The next morning, the police sent Zhu Yuting to the First Special Court for interrogation. The details have been reported previously. The day before yesterday, Judge Xiao Xiefei presided over a continued hearing in the Third Criminal Court. Chief Police Lawyer Li Zhishan stated the facts of the case. Witness Wang Jiyun then testified that he lived with the defendant and that the defendant went out to see a play at Leyi Building on Taopeng Road at 11:00 PM that night and returned at 2:45 AM, without any sign of panic. He bought and drank "Holan" water, sat and cooled down. After a while, Huang Haitang was arrested. Another witness, Zhang Jinsheng, testified that the defendant gathered many people to his house at about 6:00 AM that morning, beat him up without any reason, and said that he wanted to kill three more people, including the deceased and someone else. He said that the defendant had been violent in the past. The deceased's wife, Huang Shi, firmly stated that she had witnessed the defendant fleeing as soon as he saw her arrive, and demanded strict punishment to avenge her husband. When questioned, the defendant said that he had no grudges with the deceased and that the matter of borrowing money was completely fabricated. He said that he had a dispute with witness Zhang Jinsheng because he had opened a "Swallow's Nest" and sold opium. He claimed that Huang Haitang was assassinated and then falsely accused him of being arrested. He claimed that the morning Zhang said that he had gathered people to beat him up and wanted to kill him were all false. He hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an for his defense. After Judge Xiao verified the testimony, he ordered the defendant to be returned to custody. The debate in this case has concluded, and sentencing is scheduled.

Murder by Strangulation, Body Abandoned in Hanoi 136

Male corpse found in the Haitang Creek of Dongjiadu

On the   Haitang Creek at the southern end of the Sanguantang in Dongjiadu, Pudong, at approximately 4 PM the day before yesterday, a male corpse of unknown identity suddenly surfaced. The man had a shaved head, wore a white undershirt on his upper body, was naked below the waist, and had no shoes or socks. He suffered from eczema on his feet and appeared to be around thirty years old. A hemp rope was tied tightly around his neck, cutting deep into the flesh, clearly indicating that he had been strangled to death. However, the body was not bloated, suggesting that he was murdered on land and then dumped into the creek to cover up the crime. Passersby discovered the body and immediately reported it to the Third Precinct, Third Division for investigation. Chief Dong of the precinct determined that the incident occurred in a small creek at the boundary between the sixteenth and seventeenth districts. He then instructed the district heads Yin Bangfu and Hu Atao to report the matter to the local court for an autopsy. Yesterday at 3 PM, the court appointed Inspector Yang, accompanied by assistants, to conduct an examination in Pudong. The autopsy confirmed that the deceased had indeed been strangled to death with a rope. As no family members claimed the body, the district heads were ordered to prepare a coffin for burial while the search for the murderer continued. The creek banks are in a desolate and sparsely populated area, and there have been incidents of bandits robbing pedestrians of their money and valuables at night. It is possible that the victim was robbed of his money and clothing by bandits and then murdered to silence him. The local police station should pay close attention.

Liu Zitang Robbed in Pudong 137

Right hand already slashed

Money not taken

Liu Zitang, a native of Pudong, works as a salesman for the Chunji Knitting Factory in Shanghai. Yesterday, he went to the Zhoupu and Sanzao areas of Pudong to collect debts and sell a dozen pairs of silk stockings and gloves. He collected over three hundred silver dollars in Zhoupu. Liu then went to Xinchang to collect debts and sell goods. Suddenly, when he arrived near the Chenjiahang area northwest of Xinchang, three bandits confronted him and blocked his way, attempting to rob him. Liu resisted, and the bandits slashed him wildly with knives. A package of silk stockings and gloves carried by Liu was stolen. Fortunately, a villager passed by, and the thieves fled south with the stolen goods. Liu's right hand was slashed, but the money in his bag was not taken. This was truly a stroke of good luck amidst misfortune. Yesterday afternoon, he returned to Shanghai, reported the incident to the factory owner, and went to the hospital for treatment.

Song Yongkang Dies After Jumping From a Tram 138

Song Yongkang, a 20-year-old native of Huzhou, was a ticket seller on tram number 149 of the China General Edison Company. He joined the company on January 1st of last year and had been a diligent employee. However, during the recent (26th) typhoon and heavy rain, the company's engine room was flooded and damaged, causing all the electric lights and trams to stop running. The ticket seller, while off work, boarded a gravel-carrying truck of the China General Edison Company from the area near the South Railway Station Fire Brigade to go to the company to await orders. Unexpectedly, as the truck passed the corner of the South Railway Station and before it reached the company gate, while the truck was speeding, the ticket seller suddenly jumped off the truck, causing him to fall and injure his abdomen. His condition was critical. Company personnel immediately transported him to Guangci Hospital for treatment, but he died last night around 11 PM. The hospital notified the company, which in turn notified his family to come and collect the body.

Escaping with Gold Jewelry After Learning to Dance 139

Wang Yizai drinking tea in a tea house

Unexpectedly encounters Gu Laosi

Wang Yizai, a native of Ningbo residing at number 20 Fusheng Road in Zhabei, works as a dance instructor. A woman from Yangzhou, Gu Chen (also known as Laosi), was also learning to dance from Wang. Unexpectedly, she disappeared suddenly at 1:30 PM on the 11th of this month. When the dance student left, she was wearing a gold necklace and two gold rings. Wang Yizai had people search for her, but there was no news. At noon the day before yesterday, Wang went to a tea house at number 449 North Henan Road in the International Settlement to drink tea and unexpectedly encountered Gu Laosi. He immediately reported to Constable number 1082 and Chinese Detective Wang Runhe, who were on duty. They brought her to the Hongkou Police Station. The police chief questioned her and learned the details. He ordered her to be temporarily detained in the women's detention center and then transferred to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District the next morning. The police station's lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the facts and stated that the incident occurred in the jurisdiction of the First Sub-Precinct of the Fifth District in the Chinese area. However, the Public Security Bureau had not sent a detective to court today. Then, the plaintiff Wang Yizai briefly recounted the events. When questioned, Gu Chen confessed that she had indeed been learning to dance from Wang but refused because Wang's wife had been forcing her to entertain guests. She then returned all the gold necklace and gold rings and left. Judge Shen Bingrong verified the confession and ordered Gu Chen to be remanded in custody, pending a letter to the First Sub-Precinct of the Fifth District requesting them to send a document to pick her up.

Penalties for Illegal Construction 140

A Westerner named Cheng from the French Municipal Council criminally sued a Russian named Keli Fusi in the Second Special Court for building rental housing in the Beidang Road area. When the Municipal Council reviewed the blueprints for the permit, they modified the blueprints and instructed him to build according to the modified blueprints. He was clearly informed and signed the revised plans. However, the defendant still built according to the original blueprints, which violated the regulations of the Municipal Council. He requested that the defendant be questioned and ordered to demolish the building and rebuild it according to the revised blueprints. The defendant Keli Fusi admitted to a momentary mistake. The judge verified the confession and sentenced the defendant in court to a fine of four hundred yuan for his illegal construction. He was ordered to demolish the houses by September and build them according to the Municipal Council's blueprints.

Lost Boy Feng Dehe Awaiting Claim 141

At midnight the night before last, a boy was lost in front of the Rihua Yarn Factory in Lujiazui, Pudong, and was wandering around. The factory police intercepted him and sent him to the Third District. When questioned, the boy claimed to be Feng Dehe, ten years old, a local resident, and lived at the intersection of Caojiadu Road, about four stops away from Shanghai. Yesterday, he came to Shanghai with his foster parents to play and got separated. He heard that his foster father lived near the Baidu Bridge, but he did not know the house number. The District Head determined that there was no way to notify his family and sent him to the Public Security Bureau Lost and Found Office yesterday.

Letter to the Editor 145

To the Esteemed Editor,

We are writing on behalf of the Shanghai Mineral Ash United Business Office to express our astonishment regarding the news item in today's Shen Bao concerning the detention of mineral ash, which alleges that our office forcibly detained mineral ash belonging to Qian Renxing. Upon investigation, our office has never engaged in any such activity. Furthermore, our office serves as a joint business organization for all mineral ash traders in Shanghai and is purely commercial in nature, possessing no authority to detain goods. The report in your newspaper is clearly inaccurate, and we request that you issue a correction to avoid any misunderstandings.

Therefore, we, as representatives, urgently submit this letter, hoping that you will investigate and issue a correction to ensure accuracy.

Respectfully submitted to the Shen Bao,

Lawyer Dong Yu,

August 30th, Year 20.

Free Talk

Global Snippets 146

— Hai Ke

The World's Smallest Post Office

The world's smallest post office isn't really a post office at all. It's actually a small, painted bottle tied to a rock in the ocean, left to float on the surface. It's located in the Strait of Magellan. When ships pass by, they always send a small boat to collect the mail and place outgoing letters in the bottle. This small post office has no staff and no expenses. Yet, navies around the world protect it.

Ostrich Feathers Are Back in Style

Ostrich feathers, which were the most fashionable adornments for European and American women decades ago, are back in style this year in social circles. However, the supply is quite limited. In 1913, South Africa had an estimated 750,000 ostriches, but by 1923, production had fallen to less than half that number. In recent years, it has likely decreased even further.

In Memory of Mr. Fan Shan's Last Work 147

— Xiao

Fan Fanshan (Zengxiang) of Enshi was a master of his generation, presiding over the literary scene for decades. Sadly, he passed away from a stroke at the age of eighty-six. Mr. Zengxiang wrote over 20,000 poems in his lifetime, in addition to those already published. His last work was the *Danjing Jue Movie Song*, written last winter, dedicated to painters Qi Baishi and Lin Shixing. The song says: “The shadow play of the Song dynasty first flourished in Funing. Carved and painted figures were covered with fabric. Yan Shi controlled them to sing and dance, the sun and moon did not shine, but light was in the lamp.” (See Lu Huiqing's words to Jinggong). More than seven hundred years have passed since then. The production in the South and North is exquisite. Round heads and square feet cannot be seen, as stiff as a single layer of paper. The island nations emerged late and excelled at lascivious ingenuity, using electricity to photograph and display all shapes. Appearing on stage, one might think they are wandering in a mirror palace, with everything possessing emotion. It is a pity that the Europeans and Americans imitate the licentious Zheng and Wei, probing waists like willows, lips kissing cherries. The Japanese in the East intend to rectify the customs, striving for elegance and correctness. The Chinese are addicted to calligraphy and painting, spending millions annually to collect Wu silk. Qi Baishi drinks wine and writes poems madly, while Lin Shixing's machine hums and the lamp flickers. They use the two painters as directors, allowing the Eight Eccentrics of Yangzhou to display their abilities. Paintings within paintings, shadows within shadows, a refined pursuit promoted by Ito. Qiaolin discussed painting with Qi, and the beauties were all talented students. Qi has a white beard and exuberant spirit, Lin has curly hair and a fluffy head. Short cloth clothes tailored for Zhou Bokang, patched robes of a thin Lan Cheng. The ninth month is warm and pleasant, the east fence chrysanthemums bloom, and the sun shines. The two worthy ones take off their clothes, their energy boundless, and place the jade at the end of the stream in the middle of the courtyard. Cao Yi's and Wu Dai's styles differ, the rough and the delicate, the gods and the ghosts are amazed. Yongqiu Su Mi joins the long table, and a hundred sheets of Xuan paper are filled in a day. Once the beauty is painted, they freely inscribe and comment, and all in Runan give genuine evaluations. From entering the door to commenting on the painting, the divine skill and ingenious design require laborious operation. One painting reflects the medicine mirror, one lamp presents a shadow on the gauze screen. Each person has a state without profanity, scholars are crazy and beautiful, women are chaste. The shadow of the cicada emerges a thousand feet, Ito rolls the paper back to Tokyo. The Easterners love Fanshan's brush, regretting the lack of a Huafei Pavilion in the shadows.” The film *Danjing Jue* was filmed by Ito Weixiong of Yokohama Bank of Japan, and directed by the Chinese painters Qi Baishi and Lin Shisheng. Therefore, the poem speaks of this. Using this as a subject, if someone else were to do it, they would not know where to start. Mr. Fanshan liked to make it difficult for himself, lifting weights as if they were light. He was indeed worthy of being the leader of the literary scene. According to records, Mr. Fanshan was a Jinshi of the Xuning Dingmao period. He served as the Jiangning Administration Commissioner, where he had a good reputation for his administration, but it was all overshadowed by his reputation as a poet. After the founding of the Republic, he became a recluse in Chunming, living leisurely and rewarding and supporting actors. Many male and female actors became famous because of him. The reasons for his death this year, as rumored outside, are mostly untrue. As far as I know, Mr. Zeng attended a climb in Tianjin on the Double Ninth Festival last year at the invitation of Cao Jingyuan. After arriving in Tianjin, Mr. Chen Taoan and Mr. Xia Shouting increased his direct salary because of his age, and there was a word from Shangshu Fan. The Qing court suddenly sent letters to various newspapers, declaring it a false impersonation. Mr. Zeng was unhappy for many days. Later, his most beloved granddaughter died of illness. Mr. Zeng mourned her. From then on, his appetite decreased and his thoughts became pessimistic. Soon after, he fell and injured his foot. After healing, he fell again and could not get up. But he still did not stop composing poems. Later, he suffered from aphasia due to a stroke. The medicine was ineffective, and he passed away suddenly. Because he did not speak, there were no last words. And the last work, the *Danjing Jue Movie Song*, was written before the aphasia from the stroke while languishing in bed.

Aerial Parachuting 149

— Tian Xiang

The Aviation Sixth Team of the Aviation Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs is practicing parachute jumping. This is a very rare event in our country. Here is a brief description of the parachute jumping at that time.

In preparation for this parachute jumping practice, team leader Huang Yupai and squad leader Chen Xihong first tested it to train the team. First of all, all the pilots in the team were taught parachute theory and jumping methods by Mr. Huang. On the first day of parachute jumping practice, all pilots gathered at the airport at 2:00 p.m. to listen to all the preparations for parachute jumping before taking off.

Deep Water and Scorching Fire 150

— Jiu

Take-off. The plane for the parachute jumping practice was the Kesai No. 604. The driver was Deputy Team Leader Huang Yuquan. After the test drive was completed, Huang sat on the lower left wing and Squad Leader Chen sat on the lower right wing. They took off at 3:00 p.m., circled the city once, and flew east to the southern corner of Xiaolingwei. At that time, the plane's altitude was about 2,000 feet. Team Leaders Huang and Chen immediately jumped off the plane.

Parachute Jumping. After the parachutists left the plane, both parachutes opened simultaneously not long after. The distance was about two zhang. With the blowing of the east wind, they slowly descended in about three minutes and landed safely on the old teacher training ground. At that time, the audience applauded and cheered to express their congratulations. Deputy Team Leader Huang also drove the original plane and flew low with the two parachutes in the low altitude of the landing point. He soared until Team Leaders Huang and Chen took a car back to the airport.

Landing. The original plan was to land at Zhongshan Ao outside Zhongshan Gate. Later, after team leader Huang personally drove the plane to survey it, he recognized that there was a lot of accumulated water and many trees there, and the insurance parachute might be damaged. Therefore, it was changed to the old teacher training ground. Finally, Huang and Chen reported the situation in detail to the director and returned to the team headquarters to rest. It was already dusk.

In Memory of an Art Benefactor 151

— Zhang Shanzi

This year's floods in various provinces are unprecedented. All sectors of Shanghai are rising up to help out of neighborly friendship and disaster relief. It shows that the heart of compassion is shared by all. The artistic community is engaged in brushwork and ink cultivation, and the inkstone field is not abundant. Recently, I have followed in the footsteps of Mr. Wang Yiting, Di Chuqing, and Li Zuhan to engage in large-scale cooperation and will hold an emergency calligraphy and painting exhibition to do our best. My friend Yu Jianhua, a heroic man from Shandong, just returned from sketching in Yandang Mountain. Hearing my words, he immediately offered to donate all one hundred pieces of his third solo exhibition to help with disaster relief. It has been tentatively scheduled to be held in the lobby of the New World Hotel on September 4th, 5th, and 6th. Jianhua has been sketching in Yandang Mountain for more than a month, with its strange peaks, layered peaks, famous pools, and strange waterfalls, which has reached the great view of the world. And he has added majestic brush and ink, and a vast atmosphere, so that the painting and the mountain complement each other. He is also skilled in birds, beasts, figures, and Buddha statues, but he has kept them deeply secret, and no one knows them. Now, for the sake of disaster relief, he has exhausted all his skills. Moreover, the price is low, so that everyone can buy it. The cost is not much, but you can get exquisite masterpieces and save suffering compatriots. It is the greatest joy to do good. Why not do it? I think that at that time, they will definitely rush to be the first and be sold out in an instant. (Move the reward to help with disaster relief)

Random Thoughts on Ms. Yang Manhua's Trip to Europe (3) 152

— Ji Ping

The ambassadors and consuls dispatched by the country represent the country to the outside world. Therefore, the honor and disgrace of the ambassadors and consuls in the host country are naturally closely related to the honor and disgrace of the country. Among the ambassadors and consuls sent by our country to various European countries, how many can have international credibility and diplomatic skills? The overseas Chinese and students in Europe are very clear about this. Some people say that they are commendable for serving the public on an empty stomach and do not need strict criticism. Others say that to be an ambassador or consul in our country, one must be a capitalist who can raise funds to be competent. Otherwise, they will often be poor. How can they settle in their positions? Although the words are funny, they are also close to human nature. It is said that the poverty of embassies and consulates did not start today. However, in recent years, the situation has deteriorated. For example, when it comes to our country's National Day or major anniversaries, it is customary to invite foreign guests to hold grand ceremonies. The meaning is to celebrate the prosperity of the country and to connect with the feelings of various friendly countries. In the past, embassies and consulates must have a feast to entertain distinguished guests. Last year, due to insufficient funding, tea parties were held instead. Judging from the current situation, I am afraid that even tea parties will not be possible in the future. The country that pays the most attention to face in the international arena is Japan. They can especially save on the budget for government administrative expenses, but the funding for embassies and consulates abroad is very sufficient. Just comparing this point, we have already been dwarfed.

Few Europeans understand the situation in the East. Some people do not even distinguish between Chinese and Japanese. When they see a majestic and polite Chinese person, they open their mouths and ask (Are you Japanese?). And the relatively short Japanese are mistaken for Chinese. The Japanese take the opportunity to act stupid and theoretical, as if saying that he is Chinese is insulting to him. To be honest, the Chinese are so base that they do all kinds of evil. How can we Japanese compare to them? These people believe it to be true and almost regard the Chinese as an inferior nation. The Japanese, with ill intentions, are making trouble for us everywhere. Everyone must keep this in mind. One day, we went to a village in Belgium, and many women were fighting to see my feet. I stretched them out for them to see, and then they calmed their curiosity. One woman said. (We have never seen Chinese people before, but we have heard since childhood that Chinese people have tails. (That is, braids) They all want to marry concubines. Women all have small feet and walk with a sway. Now I understand that this is not true. Please forgive our misjudgment.) Another person who thought he was familiar with the situation in East Asia said with a mocking attitude. (How tyrannical are the Chinese warlords? There are bandits everywhere. People are living a hellish life.) He said a lot of such untrue words. I said (This kind of rumor is completely unfounded.) A gentleman who was traveling with me also responded with a very funny remark. (I think you there will know the Great Republic of China that has been established for thousands of years. After our revolution succeeds, we will simply use a microscope to illuminate your Belgium.) Then everyone laughed and dispersed. (End)

Random Notes on Northeast Exploration (7) 153

— Liu Sui Jiu

(XI) The Source of Thought

The Manchu Qing Dynasty relied on Hong Chengchou's plan to determine the world, but it also failed due to Hong's (ten no's) strategy. The power of thought is more powerful than money and guns. The Japanese are running Manchuria and Mongolia, using libraries as design rooms and the ideological system obtained from research institutes as guidelines. All agricultural and industrial development is orderly and not rashly undertaken. Even a supremely materialistic country like Soviet Russia has a (five-year plan) as a guideline for the country's entire development. Therefore, how can we despise thought or knowledge and rush to pursue money?

Libraries and schools are factories for manufacturing thought. The Japanese are running our Northeast, and libraries and schools or other research institutions related to specialized academics are the driving force behind all their Manchuria and Mongolia undertakings. In addition to the Fengtian Library in Shenyang, there is the South Manchuria Medical University. Lushun has a technical university, and Dalian has a vocational specialty school and a commercial specialty school. I once visited the South Manchuria Medical University through the introduction of Mr. Kuroda Genji. Mr. Kuroda studied in Germany for many years and obtained a doctorate. He is now a professor at the school. He teaches six hours a week at the school. He has a research room on the second floor of the school. The room is equipped with books and a blackboard. Students sometimes enter his private room to listen to lectures. He led me to visit the Chinese medicine bookstore. The four walls of bookshelves are filled with various Chinese medical books, such as the Huangdi Neijing. There are also many rare books. He earnestly guides and explains, and often expresses that the school pays special attention to the collection of Chinese medicine books. And there are achievements. There is also a huge room full of various Chinese medicinal material specimens. The names and origins are marked separately in glass bottles for storage and display. It is said that the school is specially studying the Chinese Northeast's Materia Medica. The Dalian Manchuria and Mongolia Resources Museum originally had a specialized department for scientifically testing Manchuria and Mongolia native medicinal materials. It has now been merged into the school. In previous years, I saw in the Dalian Manchuria and Mongolia Resources Museum a systematic explanation of the scientific testing of Chinese medicinal materials, so that people can know how a certain medicine is made at a glance. For example, the steps of mint making mint oil, using raw materials to display a line connecting the change system, is very simple and clear.

(XII) Northeast Thought Factory

Japanese specialized scholars are engaged in the thought manufacturing of how to run our Northeast. Their various institutions in our Northeast are engaged in specialized research on a certain problem in Manchuria and Mongolia. As for the Northeast Thought Factory on our country's side, the first to be recommended is Northeast University. However, the school's administrative aspects still need to be improved, and a concrete plan for the development of the Northeast should be urgently established.

Outside the Dadongmen of Shenyang, there is the Liaoning Provincial Library, which was founded in October of the 34th year of Guangxu. There are a total of 94,984 books. Since the librarian Bian Hongnuo took over, the organization has been quite successful. Mr. Bian is a professor at the Education Institute of Northeast University and has a great ambition to organize Northeast literature. Since I have lived in Shenyang, I have deeply felt the need to organize Northeast literature with scientific methods. I think Mr. Bian will continue to work hard. Now I heard that Mr. Bian has been transferred to the principal of the Northeast Mongolia Normal School. The former principal of the school was Mr. Guo Daofu. Mr. Guo is from Hulunbuir and was the party representative of the Mongolian Youth Party who declared independence from China during the Communist Party uprising in Hailar in previous years. Mr. Guo has been to Russia twice and can speak some Russian. He has great ambitions and wants to inherit Genghis Khan's business. At that time, he united with Russia to seek Mongolian independence. Later, Zhang Xueliang asked someone to persuade him. His thinking changed and he became anti-Russian. He took the position of Zhang's secretary and served as the principal of the Mongolian school concurrently. The Hailar problem was solved at the same time. Mr. Guo is bold, energetic and likes to talk. He comes to Northeast University to visit me from afternoon to midnight. He is the only one who speaks eloquently, all about the history of Genghis Khan. I and Mr. Li Zhenggang hosted him at Residence No. 18, Xixin Village, inside the university. Sometimes Mr. Long Bochun also sits in and drinks tea, which is a good way to relieve loneliness.

Outside the provincial library, there are 42 county libraries in the province. However, some libraries have only 400 to 500 books, while Taonan County, Tieling County, and Liaoyang County have as many as 10,000 books. Libraries and schools are both thought factories. The solution to the Chinese Northeast problem depends on these two. I further say that the competition between China and Japan in Manchuria and Mongolia is especially led by cultural undertakings.

Securities Settlement and the Weekly Bond Market Report

Only Four Days of Trading, Market Conditions Were Flat

Prices Fluctuated Slightly, Continuing a Steady Downward Trend

Last week, due to the end-of-month settlement period, there were only four days of trading, excluding Thursday and Friday when the market was closed for settlement. August futures were only traded for the first two days of the week, while October futures began trading on Saturday. Looking at the daily market performance, Tuesday was relatively active, with a volume of 22.2 million yuan. The beginning and end of the week each saw 12.13 million yuan. Wednesday was quiet, with only September futures traded, and everyone was preparing for settlement, leading to a lack of enthusiasm. The market was extremely quiet, with only a few hundred thousand yuan traded, a total of 51.085 million yuan for the whole week, a decrease of about 28 million yuan from the previous week. The internal consolidated tax was higher, at 14.005 million yuan, while the 20 Customs was at 12.8 million. Other issues were quiet, such as the 19 Customs at 6.36 million, the 20 Consolidation at 5.5 million, the Disbandment at 4.195 million yuan, the 19 Charity at 4.06 million yuan, the Demobilization at 2.72 million yuan, the 96 Public Bonds at 1.245 million yuan, the Reorganization 6% at 760,000, the Customs Duty at 400,500 yuan, and the Financial 7-Year at only tens of thousands of yuan. The spot market was also very quiet, with only 17,500 yuan traded for the entire week. Regarding the price movements of various bonds over the four days last week, the overall situation remained calm, with no changes in the bond market environment. During the settlement period, everyone was focused on settlement matters, so the market was quiet and demand was balanced. Large investors remained on the sidelines, with most activity consisting of small-scale buying and selling. Daily fluctuations were minimal. However, with the recent issuance of several new bonds, the market felt a sense of uncertainty due to supply and demand, and prices tended to fluctuate downwards. As a result, most issues were weaker compared to the previous week, with the exception of the Disbandment September issue, which fell by 1.8 yuan, and the 20 Customs September issue, which fell by 1 yuan. Other issues fell by only 0.4 to 0.5 yuan. Only the Reorganization 6%, Customs Duty, Disbandment, 19 Customs, and Charity issues saw slight increases. Looking at the bond market situation, it is likely to remain sluggish for the time being, without significant fluctuations. It is also said that the newly issued 20-Year Salt Tax Treasury Bonds will be launched at the beginning of the month. Yarn and Cotton: No Honor or Disgrace in the Yarn Market Last Week 157

Sichuan Merchants Are Currently More Active

The yarn market showed no clear signs of honor or disgrace last week, but the overall trend was very weak. Frequent floods in various regions and a serious situation have inevitably dampened autumn sales, so there are still many sellers. A certain large merchant has been actively covering his short positions in recent months, but there has been no action in the far months. The amount purchased by Rongxing Company has also remained unchanged. Both sides have considerable opposition. Midway, due to the poor surrounding environment, there was a downward trend, with each month falling by two taels. Before long, American cotton rebounded slightly, the rise in the price of grade three yarn became more intense, and the price of gold was also high. The settlement price of August standard yarn was also good, and the market showed signs of tightening. As a result, the price of standard yarn in each month was similar to the previous week, with no rise or fall. The total transaction volume was 125,500 bales. The sales of current yarn by foreign merchants were flat, but Sichuan merchants were still keen to purchase. Other merchants showed very little activity. The total amount purchased by various merchants was 5,805 bales, and 1,225 bales were purchased by fellow merchants. The market was calm. Japanese merchants opened prices for 11th and 12th month futures of 20-count Blue Phoenix Hongxi and other yarns, totaling more than 10,000 bales. The prices were relatively low. The price of grade three yarn rose by 4.5 yuan compared to the previous week. The following is a breakdown of the number of bales purchased by various merchants:

Cotton Market Rises by 6-7 Qian Last Week 158

Both Spot Cotton Arrivals and Sales are Quiet

At the beginning of last week, the cotton market was shaken by the onslaught of gales and rainstorms, and buying sentiment prevailed in the market. Short sellers showed signs of panic. At the same time, American cotton also rose slightly, and Japanese merchants made purchases, further fueling the rise. Shanghai cotton merchants had a strong bullish sentiment. Due to severe floods in various regions and low inventories of old cotton, as well as low prices for American cotton, they rushed to buy. However, the global situation remains one of oversupply, so the American cotton market remained stable with minimal fluctuations. Factories showed no interest in domestic cotton, and imports of foreign cotton continued to increase daily. The future trend will still depend on the movements of American and Indian cotton. However, most people in Shanghai believe that the floods have severely damaged the harvest, and that foreign cotton prices are fixed with too many short positions and high gold prices. Given the right opportunity, there may be a rebound. The Hankou standard price rose by 6-7 qian compared to the previous week. The total transaction volume was 462,900 dan, with no source. American cotton rose by 40 pounds compared to the previous week. The following is a breakdown of the purchase prices and number of bales of foreign cotton purchased by various factories:
