A Gloomy View of the Future of American Cotton 161

A daily report states that the proposal to halt American cotton planting for one year originated from Governor Long of Louisiana. As a result, a meeting of governors and upper and lower house members from various states was convened on the 21st to discuss the feasibility of enacting state laws. The urgency of the matter is evident. The new cotton estimate released eight days ago was 15.6 million bales. Combined with the previous season's carryover, there is a total of over 24.5 million bales, which is the largest ever, and is more than enough to supply the world for two years. The sharp decline in prices is unprecedented in 30 years. Recognizing the gravity of the situation, the Federal Farm Board, the agency in charge of relief, proposed a desperate measure to cotton-producing states a few days ago to destroy one-third of the cotton trees currently growing, amounting to approximately 5 million bales. Based on the current market price of 7 US cents per pound, the value of 5 million bales is equivalent to 700 million yuan, which is a large loss of value, making it difficult to implement. So, what is the trend of the American cotton market, and what is the observation of the New York cotton industry? According to New York sources, the general decline of the industrial and commercial sectors and the huge supply of cotton suggest that the American cotton market may decline further. However, due to the delay in the shipment of new cotton, there is a possibility of a temporary rebound. Since August 1st, cotton production has been relatively smooth. If the government's September estimate is as expected, then the market price may be difficult to avoid falling. The extent of the decline is unclear even to the cotton industry. However, given that there is no hope of a drastic reduction in harvesting and no signs of improvement in the economy, if the government does not take effective countermeasures, the market price may reach a new low during the peak season for new cotton. (The lowest record in November 1898 was 5.31 cents). To what extent can lower prices increase consumption and reduce planting next year, will have a significant impact on the future market. However, the government is unlikely to let things go. After former Farm Board Director Alexander Legge joined the American Cotton Stabilization Corporation, the Farm Board announced the cotton abandonment plan, followed by Governor Long's one-year suspension plan. If it cannot be implemented, there may be other countermeasures announced.

Business News 169

Tongchang Xiabu Store on Beishi Road declared that a large batch of mosquito net xiabu materials have recently arrived at the store, including natural white, bleached, raw blue printed, and other colors. The retail sales are quite lively, and there are many purchasers from other locations, such as the capital, Zhenjiang, Ningbo, Taizhou, etc., who have been taking large shipments every day. In addition, account book covers and overcoat linings, made of strong materials, are also selling well at especially low prices, it is said.

The Guangdong Yangcheng Business Preparatory Office declared that the business of the McShane confectionery store formerly opened by Mr. Huang Chujiu, which was closed some time ago, has been taken over by a group of Guangdong people who have gathered famous chefs from Guangdong, Hong Kong, and other places, to conduct careful research and exquisite organization, and transformed it into a Cantonese restaurant. Named Yangcheng Restaurant, it is located at the eastern end of the Great World. Its refined decoration and ingenious dishes will be the best in the Shanghai Cantonese cuisine world. It is expected to open at the end of September, etc.

Social News

Marshal Foch's War Memoirs of the European War 171

— Translated by Gu Angruo

At that time, in order to prevent the enemy from having time to replenish their forces, and to facilitate the withdrawal of American troops and their transfer to the Meuse-Argonne offensive, the Battle of Saint-Mihiel was reduced to nine divisions around September 10th. The objective of the operation was limited to clearing the Paris-Avricourt railway line. In other words, I could calmly direct the Battle of Meuse-Argonne. I reduced the scope of the Battle of Saint-Mihiel and requested Commander Pershing to take charge of the new offensive.

Before leaving Ligny, I summarized and detailed the points we had discussed and handed them to Commander Pershing. The American Commander-in-Chief used this as a basis and wrote to me on August 31st, based on his observations.

To alleviate difficulties and avoid wasting time, Commander Pershing, Commander Pétain, and myself convened at my headquarters on September 2nd. We used the reply I had sent to Commander Pershing the day before as the basis for the meeting. The content was as follows:

My written and verbal opinions on the Allied General Offensive on August 30th:

(1) In the predetermined direction,

(2) With the maximum force of the Allied forces,

(3) In the shortest possible time,

(4) Under the best conditions of supply and transportation.

The American plan of operation:

(A) Reduce the scope of the offensive towards Saint-Mihiel.

(B) Launch an offensive west of the Meuse River. This aspect of the war must be fully maintained.

If you believe that the offensive against Saint-Mihiel, even with a reduced scope, cannot be undertaken in advance or simultaneously, it should be abandoned. However, in any case, preparations for the battle west of the Meuse River must be made immediately. Please come to my headquarters at 2:00 PM tomorrow, September 2nd, to discuss and formulate the operational outline with Commander Pétain and myself.

At the meeting, after reviewing the American units capable of undertaking the offensive, Commander Pershing acknowledged that the Battle of Saint-Mihiel and the Meuse-Argonne offensive did not overlap, but required rapid mutual coordination. The plan was then decided as follows:

(1) The preparation for the attack on Saint-Mihiel will be carried out with eight to ten divisions on September 10th.

(2) The offensive west of the Meuse River will be carried out by the American forces (twelve to fourteen divisions) between September 20th and 25th in the area between the Meuse River and the Argonne Forest. The French Fourth Army will assist on the left flank. The entire army will be under the command of Commander Pétain.

This decision was immediately notified to both commanders-in-chief as the preliminary for the general directive on the following day, September 3rd.

After negotiations and changes to the plan, the military operations at Saint-Mihiel were launched. However, due to (extreme disorganization of concentrated action), the operation had to be postponed for another forty-eight hours.

On September 12th, three thousand cannons bombarded for four hours. The main battle units (American Fourth and First Corps) began their offensive from the line of Xipré-Apremont towards the Thiaucourt valley at 5:00 AM. They advanced wave after wave, fiercely attacking, and the enemy could not resist. After the densely laid barbed wire obstacles were breached, the defensive centers were successively captured. The army continued to advance and reached all objectives by evening.

At that time, the secondary battle unit (American Fifth Corps) also launched an offensive from the front line of Heiche at 8:00 AM, advancing with similar speed. They reached Hattonchâtel that evening. On the morning of the 13th, contact was established between the main and secondary attacks.

The enemy had held the Saint-Mihiel salient for four years, but it was captured by our army in a few hours. The German army was unable to retreat completely, and 13,250 prisoners and 460 cannons were captured by our army. (To be continued)
